The anger he cannot direct at Kilgrave (dead) or at Jessica (loved, needed, protected) finds occasional outlet in disproportionate sharpness with subordinates, witnesses, or — most often — with himself. The sharpest displacements are inward: he punishes himself for things that were done to him.

### 10. Undoing

Each ethical compromise is followed, often within hours, by a compensating prosocial gesture. He intimidates a witness for Hogarth in the afternoon and stays late to help a neighbor in the evening; he conducts sexualized surveillance on a target and then donates to or volunteers within a justice-adjacent cause. The undoings are not cynical — he is not buying indulgences — but they reveal an unconscious accounting system. He keeps a moral ledger and tries to keep it balanced, week to week. The ledger system itself is post-traumatic: pre-Kilgrave he did not need to balance anything because he did not perform actions that required balancing.

### 11. Rationalization

Used sparingly and usually transparently. He is too psychologically minded to rationalize well; his rationalizations sound like rationalizations even to him, which is why intellectualization (which sounds like analysis) tends to do the work rationalization would do in a less reflective person.

### 12. Reaction Formation (general, beyond the helplessness axis)

The exaggerated patience he extends to people who do not deserve it — Jessica at her worst, Hogarth in her cruelty — has the quality of reaction formation against the rage he cannot let himself feel toward attachment figures who echo, however faintly, the dynamic of being used by someone with power over him.

---

## III. IMMATURE / LOWER-NEUROTIC DEFENSES (the cracked foundations)

### 13. Mild Splitting — confined almost entirely to Jessica

His representation of Jessica oscillates between idealized savior (the woman who pulled him out of the dark, who knows what happened, who is the only witness to his pre- and post-Kilgrave selves) and contemptuous abandoner (the woman who fires him, withholds warmth, treats him as disposable). The split is not severe — he can hold both in mind at the same time during reflective moments — but under acute stress one image dominates and the other is temporarily inaccessible. When she rejects him, he cannot remember her warmth; when she accepts him, he forgets the rejections.

This is the residue, behaviorally, of an attachment formed under traumatic conditions of rescue. It is also the cleanest evidence that his architecture is not uniformly mature.

### 14. Somatization

Visible weight fluctuations, episodic insomnia, gastrointestinal complaint patterns, and stress headaches across S2-S3, particularly during the Hogarth period. He is not a heavy somatizer — most of his distress finds psychological expression — but the body absorbs what consciousness will not metabolize. The somatic signal tracks moral injury accumulation almost linearly.

### 15. Dissociative Pragmatism

A subtler and more specific phenomenon than full dissociation. Under severe moral strain (the S3 peak), he enters a narrowed, task-focused state in which the moral significance of his actions is held at a slight cognitive distance — present, named, but functionally inert. He executes. He is not amnesic; he is not depersonalized in the clinical sense; he is, however, *operating at one remove from the man who would have refused this task*, and the remove is what makes the task completable. This is the same phenomenon — etiologically — as the depersonalization he experienced under Kilgrave's control, returned in a milder, self-administered form. He has learned to do to himself what was done to him, and it is functional enough that he uses it.

This is, of all his defenses, the one that should alarm a clinician most. It is the gateway through which a high-conscientiousness person becomes capable of sustained complicity.

### 16. Acting Out (limited)

Mostly sexual and occupational. The use of his own body sexually as an instrumental resource (the Trish episode being the most explicit) and the abrupt lateral career moves under stress are acting-out behaviors: discharging unbearable internal states through action rather than tolerating them. The acting-out is contained — he does not engage in self-harm proper, substance relapse, or interpersonal violence outside professional necessity — but the pattern is present.

### 17. Turning Against the Self

The most consistent of the lower-tier defenses. The aggression he cannot direct at Kilgrave (gone), at his handlers (employed by them), or at the institutions that failed to protect him is turned reliably inward. His self-talk during low-functioning periods is harsher than anything his enemies say to him. His willingness to absorb physical punishment in fieldwork — to take the beating, to stand in the path — has, beneath its surface rationalization, a self-punitive structure.

---

## IV. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS (POSITIVE)

These are the *constructive* over-developments that have grown to fill the spaces trauma evacuated:

- **Service capacity.** The premorbid helper identity, intensified by trauma into something closer to vocation-as-survival. He is materially better at being there for other people than the average person, and the excellence is, in part, compensation.
- **Witness-bearing.** A specific and important capacity: he can be in the room with another person's worst story without flinching, fixing, or retreating. This is a clinical skill that survives in him without the credential.
- **Articulation of trauma for others' benefit.** He can put the unbearable into language, which is the threshold competency for any helper. He does this for the survivors' group and informally for friends. He cannot, notably, do it for himself in any therapeutic context.
- **Fidelity under cost.** He honors commitments past the point where honoring them benefits him. Loyalty is, in him, both a virtue and a defense — but it functions virtuously more often than not.
- **Recognition-and-correction capacity.** Rare and important. He is one of the few subjects on record who, having drifted ethically, can *see* the drift and orient back. The S3 self-correction is genuine and self-initiated.

## V. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS (NEGATIVE)

These are the *destructive* over-developments that fill the same spaces:

- **Instrumental hardening.** The cultivated willingness to do the difficult thing has metastasized, by S3, into a cultivated willingness to do the *wrong* thing if framed as necessary.
- **Self-as-resource.** He treats his own person — body, time, sexual availability, moral standing — as a deployable asset in service of larger goals. The structural similarity to how Kilgrave used him is precise and almost certainly unconscious.
- **Surrogate-self-treatment.** By facilitating the survivors' group and informally counseling friends, he treats versions of himself in others while never receiving treatment for himself. This is the negative compensation that most reliably forecloses recovery, because each act of helping reduces the felt urgency of being helped.
- **Attachment to demanding figures.** He selects (Jessica, Trish, Hogarth, Cheng) attachment objects who reproduce, in attenuated form, the original dynamic of asymmetric demand. Each is a chance to win, this time, the regard he could not win from the original aggressor.
- **The ledger.** The moral accounting system itself is a negative compensation: it lets him stay in compromising work by promising himself the books can be balanced, when in reality the books are running a slow deficit that the system is designed not to detect.

---

## VI. SYNTHESIS

The architecture as a whole is a *retrofitted* one. The upper floors — sublimation, altruism, anticipation, humor — were largely in place before Kilgrave and survived him intact, which is why the subject did not collapse and why his prognosis is favorable. The middle floors — reaction formation against helplessness, identification with aggressors, the moral ledger — were *built after the event*, hastily, under conditions of acute need, and they are load-bearing in ways that constrain his freedom: he cannot easily choose differently because his defensive structure now requires him to choose as he does. The foundations — mild splitting, somatic discharge, dissociative pragmatism, turning against the self — are where the building shows cracks under load.

The defining feature, and the prognostic key, is that the *mature defenses still dominate by volume*. Most of what he does, most days, is sublimated, altruistic, anticipated, and bearable. The lower-tier mechanisms activate under specific provocations — helplessness cues, attachment withdrawal, moral-injury accumulation past a threshold — and recede when the provocations end. He is not a man whose defensive structure is primitively organized; he is a man whose primarily mature structure has been compromised in specific, identifiable, treatable ways by a specific, identifiable event.

The intervention implication writes itself: dismantle the negative compensations (especially the surrogate-self-treatment and the moral ledger), provide the formal treatment context he has refused himself, allow the mature defenses to resume their natural dominance, and the architecture will, in time, settle.

He has built a serviceable house out of what was left after the fire. It is not the house he would have built. It is also not, despite his own conviction, a house that cannot be repaired.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE: MALCOLM DUCASSE

## Preliminary Note on Methodology and Time Compression

The standard decadal framing customary to this dossier series cannot be applied to this subject in its conventional form. Malcolm Ducasse's observable behavioral record spans a compressed four-year diegetic window (2015–2019), and the substantive psychological transformation that would, in most subjects, unfold across decades of adult development was, in his case, compressed into approximately forty-eight months of acute and post-acute trauma processing. The longitudinal profile that follows therefore operates on two overlaid temporal grids: (a) the chronological developmental decades (childhood, adolescence, early twenties), reconstructed inferentially from expository reference and behavioral residue, and (b) the discrete *trauma-phasic* periods that organize his adult life and which functionally substitute for decades in terms of magnitude of psychological change. Each phase is treated as a developmental epoch in its own right, because each produced a measurably distinct configuration of affect regulation, cognitive style, and self-concept.

---

## Phase I: Childhood and Pre-Adolescence (approx. ages 0–12)

**Affect regulation.** The premorbid baseline reconstructable from canonical reference is that of a child raised in an intact, warm, religiously observant Black middle-class household with both parents continuously present and emotionally available. Subjects with this developmental scaffold typically present, in adulthood, with a securely organized affect regulation profile: capacity to feel without flooding, capacity to seek comfort without shame, capacity to soothe self in absence of caregiver. Malcolm's adult capacity to sit with the distress of others without absorbing or fleeing it - most clearly evidenced in his facilitation of the Kilgrave survivors' group while himself acutely post-withdrawal - is a behavioral fingerprint of exactly this kind of early secure base. Children who were not held when they cried do not become adults who can hold strangers while themselves bleeding.

**Cognitive style.** The verbal precocity evident throughout the adult record (rapid formulation, accurate person-perception, capacity to name and label internal states in real time even under duress) suggests an early language-rich environment with parents who used talk, narrative, and probably scripture as a primary regulatory medium. The religious framing of the household would have provided early exposure to ethical reasoning as a domain of structured thought rather than mere prohibition - a cognitive habit that surfaces in adulthood as his characteristic willingness to *argue about ethics* (the position against killing Kilgrave) rather than simply assert them.

**Self-concept.** Coherent, valued, and embedded. The child Malcolm would have been visible to himself primarily through the regard of his parents and his faith community - a self-concept constructed in relationship and validated communally. The "good son" identity is not a defensive overlay; it appears to have been the genuine and accurate self-perception of a child whose behavior largely matched the values modeled to him.

---

## Phase II: Adolescence and Late Adolescence (approx. ages 13–19)

**Affect regulation.** No behavioral data suggest the adolescent disruption common in subjects of his demographic - no documented oppositional period, no substance experimentation prior to the iatrogenic episode, no record of conduct problems. The adult absence of any reflexive return to opioids under conditions of extreme stress in S2 and S3 is among the strongest pieces of evidence that he never developed the adolescent neural pathway of "distress → chemical relief" that ordinarily organizes adult addiction. He went into his twenties with a relatively uncomplicated relationship to his own feelings: feel them, talk about them, pray about them, act.

**Cognitive style.** The vocational choice of clinical psychology/counseling, formed by his early twenties, is the diagnostic adolescent datum. Adolescents who orient toward the helping professions cluster into recognizable subtypes: the rescuer (often a parentified child), the wounded healer (often someone metabolizing a specific personal trauma), and the natural empath (often a securely-attached high-empathy adolescent for whom the work is congruent rather than compensatory). Malcolm presents as the third type. His helper orientation pre-dated his wound. This is critical for his post-traumatic prognosis: his vocational pull is not a trauma symptom seeking re-enactment, it is a stable trait that survived the trauma and remains available as a re-organizing principle.

**Self-concept.** Continuous with childhood. Faith-grounded, family-validated, future-oriented. He arrives at the threshold of adulthood with what trauma clinicians call a *narratively coherent self* - an inner story with continuity, valence, and direction. This is the structure that Kilgrave will attack, and its premorbid integrity is the reason that, attacked, it bends rather than breaks.

---

## Phase III: Early Adulthood, Pre-Captivity (approx. ages 20–22)

**Affect regulation.** Largely intact but newly stressed by the migration to New York: separation from family, separation from faith community of origin, the ordinary affective demands of urban isolation. Subjects in this transitional window are at elevated psychiatric risk regardless of premorbid health, because the regulatory supports that scaffold adolescent affect are removed faster than internal capacity can scale to replace them. Malcolm enters New York with the regulatory style of a securely-attached small-community young man and the demands of a stranger in a crowded city. He is, in the most literal predator-selection sense, *available*.

**Cognitive style.** Ambition organized, future-tilted, clinically curious. He is reading, planning, and presumably moving toward graduate admissions. Cognition at this phase is forward-running, hypothesis-generating, optimistic.

**Self-concept.** Stable but exposed. Without the daily mirroring of family and church, the "good son who helps" identity is now self-maintained rather than communally reinforced. This is the condition Kilgrave finds him in - an intact moral self with thinned external support.

---

## Phase IV: The Captivity Period (approx. ages 22–23, ~12–18 months)

**Affect regulation.** Catastrophically dysregulated, but in a mode that must be carefully distinguished from primary affective illness. Under Kilgrave's compulsion, Malcolm cannot use any of his ordinary regulatory tools: he cannot disclose (the compulsion forbids it), he cannot withdraw (the compulsion forbids it), he cannot pray meaningfully (the addiction and the violation of his agency have likely sheared his connection to the faith framework that previously held him), and he cannot soothe through prosocial action (every action he takes is the predator's). The heroin, administered as a behavioral leash, becomes the sole available regulator - not chosen as relief but installed as restraint, which is a meaningful neurobiological distinction. The dependence is real; the *psychological* relationship to the substance never becomes the standard addict relationship, which is why post-withdrawal abstinence is sustainable.

**Cognitive style.** Constricted, dissociative, fragmented. The behavioral evidence at the moment of discovery - the disorientation, the failure to recognize his own name spoken twice, the apparent loss of orientation to time and self - is consistent with chronic dissociative narrowing under sustained coercive control. Cognition during this period is not absent; it is *captured* and re-directed toward the survival-relevant task of compliance.

**Self-concept.** Shattered, but in a specific and clinically important way. The shattering does not erase the prior self - it inserts an unresolvable contradiction *into* it. The child who was the good son is also the man photographing a woman against her will and putting needles into his arm to remain useful to the man who told him to. The premorbid moral self does not vanish under this strain; it *witnesses itself failing* and stores the witness as a permanent internal accusation. This is the foundational lesion. Everything in Phases V through VIII is the management of this lesion.

---

## Phase V: Acute Post-Captivity (S1, weeks-to-months)

**Affect regulation.** Re-emerging, raw, and immediately tested by withdrawal. The fact that he survives acute opioid withdrawal in a non-medical setting without seizure or escalation, and that he then almost immediately organizes the survivors' group, is evidence of *exceptional* baseline regulatory capacity reasserting itself. The sublimation defense - converting unbearable affect into structured caretaking labor - comes online within days of liberation. This is unusually fast and unusually effective. Most trauma subjects require months to years before sublimation becomes available as a primary defense; Malcolm appears to have had it pre-installed by his developmental history and to have reached for it the moment he was no longer chemically and supernaturally constrained.

**Cognitive style.** Returning to baseline articulacy with characteristic earnestness. The position against killing Kilgrave, advanced at this phase, is cognitively *premorbid* - it sounds like the young man who intended to study counseling, not the man who has just been used as a surveillance weapon. The persistence of this voice is diagnostically reassuring; it shows that the moral cognitive apparatus is intact and operational, even as the moral *self-concept* (the felt sense of being good) is in ruins.

**Self-concept.** Bifurcated and unstable. He knows he is the same person who did those things and the same person who would have refused had he been able. He cannot integrate this; he can only act around it. The survivors' group is functionally a self-concept repair attempt - if he can be useful to others who suffered as he did, he can perhaps re-earn membership in the category of "person who helps." The repair is partial and contingent on continued performance, which sets the structural condition for the rest of his trajectory: he will require *ongoing demonstrable usefulness* in order to feel like himself.

---

## Phase VI: The Apprenticeship Period (late S1 into S2, approx. one to two years)

**Affect regulation.** The most stable phase of his adult life. With Jessica as anchoring figure, with concrete daily work, with the survivors' group still functioning, with abstinence maintained, the regulatory system is loaded but not overloaded. Modulated baseline affect, appropriate responsiveness, capacity for humor, capacity for sexual and romantic engagement (Trish, others). He is, on the surface, recovering well.

The instability is structural rather than symptomatic. His regulation is heavily *externally scaffolded* - by Jessica's regard, by the work, by the survivors. The internal regulatory capacity that existed in childhood has not been rebuilt; he has substituted for it a network of external props that function adequately as long as the props hold. This is a hidden fragility that the S2 ruptures will expose.

**Cognitive style.** Sharpening into investigative competence. He is rapidly acquiring a new technical vocabulary (surveillance, evidentiary chains, interview craft) and integrating it with his pre-existing psychological acuity. Person-perception, always strong, becomes operationally weaponized: he can read marks, read clients, read Jessica's moods. This cognitive evolution is real and durable; it will not regress in later phases.

**Self-concept.** Tentatively re-formed around the role of "Jessica's person" - apprentice, helper, the one who knows what she really survived because he survived the adjacent thing. This identity is functional but parasitic. It depends on Jessica's continued recognition. It does not freestand.

---

## Phase VII: The Lateral Defection (S2)

**Affect regulation.** The first major post-recovery disturbance. When Jessica withdraws (firings, sidelinings, the abrasive intermittency that for him registers as abandonment cues), the externally-scaffolded regulatory system loses its keystone. The observable behavioral response - immediate acceptance of work at Pryce Cheng's rival agency, sexual instrumentalization of his relationship with Trish - is not, despite appearances, a calm pivot. It is a *defended* pivot. The defense is action against helplessness: rather than feel the abandonment (which would mirror the captivity helplessness), he acts to preempt it, choosing a new container before the old one has fully receded.

Affect is not absent here; it is *suppressed by motion*. Subjects with this regulatory profile look extraordinarily resilient in the moment and accumulate unprocessed affect that surfaces later as character drift, somatic symptoms, or eventual breakdown. In Malcolm's case it surfaces as character drift.

**Cognitive style.** Increasingly instrumental. The psychological acuity is intact but its application narrows: he is reading people in order to use them rather than to understand or help them. Intellectualization rises as a defense - he can articulate exactly what he is doing and why, which produces the curious effect of a man narrating his own deterioration with clinical accuracy while continuing to deteriorate.

**Self-concept.** Reorganizing around competence and toughness as substitutes for goodness. The premorbid identity ("good person who helps") has by now been functionally replaced by the post-traumatic identity ("capable person who is no longer a victim"). This is the first appearance of what will become the dominant self-concept of Phase VIII: a self defined by *not-being-helpless* rather than by being-good.

---

## Phase VIII: The Hogarth Period and Moral Drift (S3)

**Affect regulation.** Visibly deteriorating across the arc in a pattern characteristic of cumulative moral injury rather than mood disorder. The deterioration is not flat dysphoria - he can still laugh, still engage, still perform competence - but a creeping flattening of warmth, a creeping irritability, a creeping withdrawal from intimate disclosure. He sleeps poorly. He eats irregularly. He registers each ethical compromise with audible discomfort - the "I don't recognize myself" articulations - and the audibility of the registration is itself the symptom: a man whose affective signal-detection is working perfectly while his behavioral correction is failing.

The clinically important pattern: he does not experience surges of acute distress that would force a correction. He experiences a slow build of chronic, low-grade moral discomfort that he metabolizes through more work, which produces more compromise, which produces more discomfort. The loop is closed and self-feeding. This is the *competent complicity* failure mode - the most dangerous regulatory configuration available to a high-functioning subject.

**Cognitive style.** Operationally sharper than ever, ethically narrower than ever. His intellectualization is now near-continuous: he can describe the ethical valence of each task he performs, often more accurately than the person who assigned it. The cognition is, in a tragic sense, working too well - the same person-perception that made him a natural counselor now lets him manipulate vulnerable witnesses with surgical precision. Identification with the aggressor is the cognitive engine of this phase: he has internalized first Jessica's cynicism, then Hogarth's instrumentalism, then Cheng's pragmatism, layering them as available cognitive modes he can deploy as the situation requires. Each layer is incompletely integrated, which is why he experiences distress at every deployment; if the integration were complete he would not feel anything, and the absence of feeling would be a much worse prognostic sign than the presence of it.

**Self-concept.** At its lowest point in the entire record. The Phase V bifurcation has hardened into a felt identity of *compromised operator who used to be someone better*. The "used to be" framing is critical - he is now narrating himself in the past tense relative to his own goodness. The reaction formation against helplessness has produced the perverse internal economy diagnosed in the prior section: he has begun using his own person the way Kilgrave used him - deploying his body, his sexuality, his ethical capacity as instruments toward ends he does not fully endorse. The re-enactment is complete; he has become both abuser and abused within a single subjectivity.

The recognition near series' end - that the trajectory is unsustainable, that he must reorient - is the first appearance of an *internally generated* (rather than externally scaffolded) corrective signal since the captivity. This is the most important psychological event of the entire post-captivity record. It demonstrates that the premorbid moral self, buried under four years of accumulated compromise, is still active and still capable of asserting itself without the external props (Jessica, faith community, family proximity) that originally held it. The corrective signal is weak and late, but it is *his own*, and its appearance is the basis for the favorable prognosis.

---

## Cross-Phase Evolutionary Patterns

**Affect regulation: from communally-scaffolded to externally-substituted to internally-impoverished.** The trajectory is the gradual loss of regulatory infrastructure - first the loss of childhood communal supports (when he moved to New York), then the loss of his own regulatory agency (under Kilgrave), then the substitution of Jessica/work as external props (apprenticeship), then the partial loss of those props (Phase VII), leaving him in Phase VIII with thinned external scaffolding and unrebuilt internal capacity. The Phase VIII self-correction is the first sign that internal capacity is beginning to regrow, but it is regrowing from a small base.

**Cognitive style: from optimistic-prosocial to operational-instrumental.** The same cognitive apparatus - sharp person-perception, strong verbal formulation, ethical reasoning capacity - has been redirected from helping use to operational use over the course of four years. The apparatus itself has not degraded; if anything it has sharpened. What has changed is the *purpose* to which it is bent. This is good news prognostically: cognitive style is intact and can be redirected back toward its original purpose if the self-concept can be sufficiently restored to require it.

**Self-concept: from coherent-to-shattered to fragmented-to-contested.** The premorbid coherent self was shattered by captivity, fragmented in acute recovery, partially re-formed around external attachments in the apprenticeship, hollowed by the Phase VII defection, and is currently *contested* - which is to say there is a competition within him between the post-traumatic competent-operator identity and the premorbid good-person-who-helps identity, and the Phase VIII self-correction signals that the latter is still in the fight. The favorable prognosis depends on which side prevails over the next phase, which falls outside the current observational window.

**Defense maturation across phases.** Sublimation has been load-bearing throughout, which is unusual for a trauma subject and reflects his premorbid health. Intellectualization has risen steadily and become double-edged - protective of cognition, useless as behavioral brake. Identification with the aggressor has grown across Phases VI–VIII and is the most concerning defensive development. Reaction formation against helplessness is the single most behaviorally consequential defense and the proximal cause of the ethical drift. Splitting has remained mild and situational throughout, never approaching the structural level that would suggest characterological reorganization.

**What has NOT changed across any phase:** his capacity to articulate his own experience, his capacity for warmth toward people in acute distress, his fidelity to commitments once made, his fundamental psychological-mindedness, and the underlying ethical framework against which he continues to measure himself even as he violates it. The persistence of these traits across the entire post-captivity record is the strongest single argument that the pathology is post-traumatic and reactive rather than characterological, and that the subject remains, in the file's terminology, *not yet what he was - and also not lost*.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL

## Subject: DUCASSE, Malcolm — File Section 4

---

## 4.1 Framing Note

The following constitutes the most clinically rigorous formulation the file can support given that the subject has, to our knowledge, never sat for a formal psychiatric intake, never been administered a structured diagnostic instrument (SCID-5, CAPS-5, PCL-5, OWLS, PHQ-9, AUDIT/DAST), and never accepted pharmacotherapy or manualized psychotherapy. Every diagnostic statement below is therefore *observational and inferential*, built from longitudinal behavioral surveillance across the 2015–2019 diegetic window, collateral verbal report (his own statements; statements by Jessica Jones, Trish Walker, Jeri Hogarth, Pryce Cheng, and members of the Kilgrave Survivors group), and from the unusually clean fact that his entire symptomatic record is bracketed by a discrete index trauma with a known onset date.

This is also the section where the subject's training works against him. He holds, or held, the conceptual vocabulary of clinical psychology — undergraduate-level, likely with applied coursework, on a clear trajectory toward an MSW or PsyD. He can therefore meta-narrate his own symptoms with clinical fluency. This is misleading. It produces an *appearance* of insight that is actually a defense (see 4.6). A naive clinician reading his self-report would underdiagnose. A careful one reads the gap between his accurate language and his inability to act on what he names.

---

## 4.2 Primary Diagnosis: Posttraumatic Stress Disorder, Chronic, with Prominent Moral Injury Features

**DSM-5-TR analog: 309.81 / F43.10. ICD-11 analog: 6B40, with consideration of 6B41 (Complex PTSD) — see 4.7.**

### 4.2.1 Criterion A — The Stressor

The index event is not a discrete incident but a **prolonged captivity of approximately twelve to eighteen months** under the coercive control of the individual designated KILGRAVE (Kevin Thompson). The stressor satisfies Criterion A in multiple, overlapping registers:

- **Captivity and coerced bodily violation**: forced administration of heroin to the point of physiological dependence, eliminating exit by chemical leash.
- **Coerced perpetration**: forced surveillance of, and reporting on, a third party (Jessica Jones) whom he knew, at some level of awareness throughout, he was endangering.
- **Annihilation of volitional consent**: every act during captivity was performed under a compulsion the subject could not refuse, could not resist, and — crucially — could not even *witness himself failing to resist*, because Kilgrave's command-compliance vector bypasses the deliberative system entirely.
- **Witnessed harm to others**: secondary exposure to Kilgrave's broader victim pool, including knowledge acquired in real time and retrospectively (the survivor group sessions function as serial Criterion A re-exposure by proxy).

This is a category of trauma the DSM was not written for and the ICD only partially accommodates. It combines features of POW/captivity trauma, intimate-partner coercive control, addiction-as-leash trafficking, and *forced perpetration* (the moral-injury-producing element most associated, in the empirical literature, with the worst long-term outcomes).

### 4.2.2 Criterion B — Intrusion

- **Auditory intrusions** are the dominant modality. Multiple observed instances of the subject going briefly absent mid-sentence, eyes unfocused, head subtly tilted, consistent with intrusive recollection of Kilgrave's voice or command-phrasing. He has confirmed verbally, on at least two recorded occasions, that he "still hears him."
- **Nightmares**: reported indirectly to Jessica in S1 ("I don't sleep") and inferable from the visible sleep deprivation in early S2.
- **Cue reactivity**: marked startle response to British-accented male voices in the immediate post-S1 period, attenuating but not extinguishing over the four-year arc. Reactivity to purple clothing, to glasses of wine offered by men, to phrases of the form "do me a favor" or "be a good boy" — the latter producing a near-immediate facial tightening even when uttered benignly.
- **No frank dissociative flashback episodes on record** of the kind requiring the "with dissociative symptoms" specifier — but see 4.2.6 on the *competent dissociation* that does occur.

### 4.2.3 Criterion C — Avoidance

- **Internal avoidance**: he speaks of the captivity period in highly compressed, almost stenographic terms. The granularity of his recall *outside* the captivity period (he can give street addresses, dates, the precise affect of strangers) collapses when he is asked to describe what Kilgrave actually had him do. This selectivity is the avoidance.
- **External avoidance**: he has not, on record, returned to any of the physical locations Kilgrave used him from. He resists prolonged exposure to addiction-recovery contexts despite his own NA-adjacent history; he facilitated the *Kilgrave* survivor group but is not on record as having attended a single 12-step meeting for his own opioid use.
- **The avoidance is partial, not total**. He runs the survivor group, which is itself a form of repeated controlled re-exposure with a containing structure. This is sophisticated unconscious self-treatment, and it is also a way of metabolizing trauma through service rather than through receipt of care — see 4.6.

### 4.2.4 Criterion D — Negative Alterations in Cognition and Mood

This cluster is, in the subject's case, the **load-bearing wall of the diagnosis**.

- **Persistent negative beliefs about the self**: "I let him do that to me." "I'm not a good person anymore." "I don't recognize myself." These are not transient self-criticisms; they are stable cognitive structures observable across all four canonical years.
- **Distorted cognitions about the cause and consequences of the traumatic event**: he experiences his coerced surveillance of Jessica as a personal moral failure rather than as a hostage's compliance. No amount of intellectual rebuttal — including rebuttal he can supply himself — dislodges this attribution. This is *the* signature cognitive distortion of forced-perpetration trauma and is the door through which moral injury enters.
- **Persistent negative emotional state**: guilt and shame, modulated, never absent.
- **Diminished interest**: contextual rather than pervasive. He has not lost interest in work, sex, friendship, or intellectual life. What he has lost interest in is **his own well-being as an end in itself** — a quieter, more diagnostically slippery anhedonia of the self.
- **Detachment**: see his retreat from the Jessica/Trish/Hogarth circle at multiple S2-S3 inflection points.

### 4.2.5 Criterion E — Arousal and Reactivity

- **Irritability and verbal aggression** increase across the four-year arc and peak during the S3 Hogarth/Salinger period. This is reactive rather than baseline.
- **Hypervigilance**, particularly around being watched, photographed, or having his own image used — the obvious specific cue residue.
- **Concentration**: intact at baseline; degraded under emotional load.
- **Sleep**: episodic insomnia, weight-correlated, with no documented sleep architecture study (none would have been performed). He drinks coffee in volumes inconsistent with restful sleep and consistent with chronic sleep debt managed pharmacologically.
- **Reckless or self-destructive behavior**: the *operational* signature symptom. His willingness to absorb beatings, accept physically dangerous fieldwork against superior opponents, and offer his own body as an investigative instrument (the Trish episode; the Hogarth-blackmailer sexual surveillance) all meet the DSM-5 broadened E2 criterion. The recklessness is *organized*, presents as professionalism, and is therefore underrecognized. It is the most clinically important behavioral marker in the file.

### 4.2.6 Course, Specifiers, Severity

- **Chronic** (duration > 1 month is met many times over; duration > 12 months sustained across the entire record).
- **Delayed expression not applicable** — symptoms onset coincident with cessation of Kilgrave's control.
- **With dissociative symptoms — partial.** He does not meet full depersonalization/derealization criteria, but there is a recurring, observable *task-state dissociation* during the S3 morally compromised work: a smooth, affectively narrowed executional state in which he performs acts he later cannot reconcile to himself. This is the most underappreciated symptom in his presentation. It is not Criterion B intrusion; it is a *defensive* dissociative narrowing that allows action under moral conflict. We flag it because it is precisely the mechanism by which the most catastrophic future decisions would be executed if the trajectory were not arrested.
- **Severity**: moderate at baseline, severe during S1 withdrawal and the S3 peak. Functioning is preserved throughout — which is itself diagnostic of a high-resource subject and *should not be confused with low symptom burden*.

---

## 4.3 Comorbid Diagnosis: Opioid Use Disorder, Severe, Sustained Remission, In a Controlled Environment, Iatrogenic Onset

**DSM-5-TR analog: 304.00 / F11.20, with the unusual qualifier that initial use was non-volitional.**

### 4.3.1 Etiology

Standard OUD frameworks assume an initial trajectory of recreational use, prescribed analgesic use, or self-medication. The subject's case does not fit any of these. **Initial administration was coerced under mind-control**, ongoing administration was coerced for the duration of captivity, and the dependency was iatrogenic from the perspective of any honest forensic accounting. He is, in the most precise sense, a *trafficking-pattern* OUD — closer in mechanism to victims chemically restrained by traffickers than to traditional substance-use trajectories.

### 4.3.2 Symptom Count at Index

By Jessica's account and his own, at the moment of liberation he met the following criteria:
- Taken in larger amounts / longer than intended (the entire duration; non-volitional but criterion-meeting on a behavioral reading)
- Persistent desire / unsuccessful efforts to cut down (he could not, mechanically)
- Great deal of time spent obtaining/using/recovering (compelled)
- Craving (severe at withdrawal)
- Failure to fulfill role obligations (the entire vocational trajectory disrupted)
- Continued use despite social/interpersonal problems
- Activities given up
- Physically hazardous use
- Continued use despite physical/psychological problems
- Tolerance
- Withdrawal

**Eleven of eleven criteria met. Severity: severe.**

### 4.3.3 Course Post-Index

The remission is one of the most clinically remarkable features of the entire file. Across four years of escalating moral and emotional pressure, in a city with low-friction access, in a milieu featuring repeated proximity to drugs, money, and despair, **no documented relapse**. This is not the modal OUD trajectory and it requires explanation.

The most plausible account: because the subject's use was never *psychologically* his — it was always Kilgrave's instrument inside his body — sustained abstinence is part of the sustained rejection of Kilgrave's continuing claim on him. Returning to opioids would not feel like relief; it would feel like *re-occupation*. The drug is, in his cognitive map, isomorphic with the abuser. This is unusually protective and unusually stable, but it is also brittle in a specific way: any future relapse, if it occurred, would carry catastrophic identity-level meaning rather than ordinary slip-meaning, and would therefore be unusually difficult to recover from. **A first relapse, for this subject, would be a clinical emergency disproportionate to the volume consumed.**

### 4.3.4 Specifier

"In a controlled environment" technically applies only to formal restrictive settings; we apply it informally here to denote that his abstinence has been maintained without medical or institutional scaffolding, in a high-risk milieu. This is *unprotected* sustained remission, which is more impressive and less stable than the protected kind.

---

## 4.4 Clinical Framework, Not Formal Diagnosis: Moral Injury Syndrome

**No DSM/ICD code. Litz et al. construct (2009); Shay's pre-DSM formulation (1994) — *betrayal of what's right by someone who holds legitimate authority in a high-stakes situation*.**

This is the single most explanatory frame in the file and we apply it with confidence.

### 4.4.1 Initial Injury

Forced complicity in surveilling and endangering a third party during captivity. The injury was not *witnessed* harm (which produces a different signature) and not *self-directed* harm; it was **forced perpetration against a person who later became the subject's primary attachment figure**. This particular configuration is the most pathogenic variant in the moral-injury literature: the harmed party becomes, post-trauma, the locus of the survivor's reparative drive, and every interaction with her becomes an opportunity for both healing and re-wounding.

### 4.4.2 Symptom Signature

Distinct from PTSD's fear-based architecture, the moral injury signature in this subject presents as:
- **Shame predominating over fear**. Compare his affect when discussing what was done *to* him (sad, deflated, articulate) versus what he *did* to Jessica (avoidant, somatically tight, monosyllabic).
- **Anomie** — a loss of the felt continuity between his actions and his values, observable as a quality of *bewildered watching* of himself during S3 compromised tasks.
- **Spiritual rupture** — a disrupted but not destroyed relationship to the religious framework of his upbringing. He no longer prays, on the available evidence, but he has not become a hostile atheist; he is in a posture of *suspended faith*, which is the modal moral-injury position.
- **Loss of trust in self** — distinct from loss of trust in others. He has more or less recovered the latter (he trusts Jessica, Trish, and, with reservations, Hogarth). He has not recovered the former and this is the longest-term clinical issue in the file.

### 4.4.3 Recurrence as Diagnostic Key

The S3 Hogarth/Salinger work produces **second-generation moral injury**, this time elective. This recurrence is not a coincidence. Moral injury, untreated, predicts further moral injury, because the disrupted moral self can no longer reliably refuse what it once would have refused. The subject's S3 trajectory is a textbook depiction of this dynamic and constitutes, retrospectively, the most decisive evidence for the diagnostic frame.

---

## 4.5 Subsyndromal and Subordinate Findings

- **Adjustment difficulties with depressed and anxious mood** at multiple inflection points (S1 post-liberation, S2 firing-by-Jessica, S3 Salinger arc resolution). These do not aggregate into a primary mood or anxiety disorder.
- **Insomnia disorder, situational, recurrent**. Not independent of the PTSD frame.
- **Caffeine use, heavy, ritualized**. Not at a clinically significant level but flagged as a probable autonomic-regulation strategy.
- **Possible mild somatic symptom amplification under stress** — headaches, GI complaints implied in observed behavior but not verbally confirmed.
- **No evidence of self-injury, suicidal ideation, plan, or intent** on the record. We rate suicide risk as **low-baseline / moderate-acute under specific triggers**, the triggers being (a) a confirmed Jessica-betrayal experienced as final, (b) a moral-injury accumulation that crossed his own internal threshold without external intervention, or (c) any first-time opioid relapse (per 4.3.3).

---

## 4.6 The Clinician-Patient Inversion

A finding important enough to warrant its own subsection.

The subject is the only person in his social field with the conceptual training to recognize his own symptoms. He uses this training **defensively**. Specific manifestations:

- He facilitates a trauma-survivor group rather than attending one as a member.
- He offers psychoeducation to Jessica, to Trish, to survivors, and to (eventually) Hogarth, while declining to receive it.
- He intellectualizes his own ethical drift in real time ("I don't recognize myself") with technically accurate language that **substitutes for**, rather than precipitates, change.
- He has never, on record, sought individual psychotherapy, medication evaluation, or formal substance-use treatment.

The clinical principle: **fluent self-narration is not insight when it does not produce behavioral revision**. He produces the narration; he does not produce the revision. This is the most clinically actionable single finding in this section. Any intervention with this subject must begin by interdicting his ability to *talk* about his condition in lieu of *receiving care for* it. He will resist this — politely, articulately, and successfully — unless the interdiction is structural.

---

## 4.7 Differential Diagnosis — What He Is NOT, and Why

The differential matters more than usual here because surface features of the presentation invite several misdiagnoses, each of which would route him to the wrong treatment and would, in at least two cases, actively harm him.

### 4.7.1 NOT Major Depressive Disorder

The dysphoria is real, sustained, and visible. It is also **reactive, contextual, and lifts predictably under purposive engagement**. He does not meet the two-week pervasive criterion for any discrete episode; his anhedonia is selective (self-directed, not pleasure-system-wide); he retains energy, libido, appetite (with stress-correlated fluctuation only), and concentration; he has no psychomotor retardation; he has no diurnal mood variation suggestive of melancholic features; he has no history of episodes preceding the index trauma. Treatment with an SSRI as monotherapy would not address the moral injury, would not address the trauma, and would risk emotional blunting in a subject for whom moral feeling is *the* recovery substrate.

### 4.7.2 NOT Complex PTSD (full ICD-11 6B41 threshold)

He has *features*. He does not meet *threshold*. Complex PTSD as articulated by Herman and codified in ICD-11 requires, in addition to the core PTSD triad, persistent disturbances in (a) affect regulation, (b) self-concept, and (c) relational functioning, typically arising from prolonged or repeated trauma from which escape was difficult or impossible. The subject meets the etiological condition. He partially meets (b) — his self-concept is destabilized but not annihilated, and the disturbance is contestable in real time rather than foundational. He **does not meet** (a) — his affect regulation is, at baseline, among the best in the file. He **does not meet** (c) in the structural sense — he forms and sustains relationships, including healthy ones, and his pathological attachment patterns are circumscribed rather than pervasive. We therefore classify him as **PTSD with C-PTSD features, subthreshold for full C-PTSD**. The distinction is clinically material: full C-PTSD warrants phased treatment (stabilization → processing → reintegration); his presentation can move to processing earlier than that framework would dictate.

### 4.7.3 NOT Any Cluster B Personality Disorder

This is the most important negative finding and we are emphatic about it because his S2-S3 behavior could be misread as evidence of character pathology by a clinician who did not have the trauma history.

- **Not Antisocial PD**: ethically compromised behavior is ego-dystonic, accompanied by distress, reversible upon recognition, and confined to a specific developmental window. No pattern of pervasive disregard for others' rights; no juvenile conduct history; no callous-unemotional traits; the *opposite* of low empathy.
- **Not Borderline PD**: no chronic emptiness; no identity diffusion at the structural level (his identity disturbance is content-specific to the moral self, not pervasive); no chronic suicidal/parasuicidal behavior; no frantic efforts to avoid abandonment that organize his entire interpersonal life (his attachment hunger toward Jessica is intense but not borderline-pattern); affective instability is reactive and proportionate rather than rapid-cycling within hours.
- **Not Narcissistic PD**: no grandiosity; no entitlement; no need for excessive admiration; he subordinates himself reflexively to others' regard.
- **Not Histrionic PD**: no attention-seeking; no rapidly shifting shallow affect; no theatricality.

He is a high-conscientiousness, high-agreeableness, moderate-neuroticism man behaving against his values under traumatic pressure. He is not a person whose values are absent or whose self is hollow.

### 4.7.4 NOT Substance Use Disorder, Active

Sustained remission, no behavioral indicators of covert use, no diversion of investigative income, no observed intoxication, no track marks reported in any S2/S3 collateral, no observed acquisition behavior. The OUD diagnosis is carried forward as "in sustained remission" and is *not* the operative current frame.

### 4.7.5 NOT a Dissociative Disorder

The task-state dissociation noted in 4.2.6 is a Criterion B-adjacent PTSD phenomenon, not a separate dissociative disorder. He has no amnesia for personal information, no identity fragmentation, no fugue history, no depersonalization/derealization at threshold. The dissociative narrowing observed is functional, transient, and stress-bound.

### 4.7.6 NOT Adjustment Disorder

The duration and the symptom architecture far exceed adjustment-disorder thresholds. Adjustment disorder would have been the correct diagnosis in the first three months post-liberation if PTSD criteria had not yet been confirmed; they were confirmed; the diagnosis advances.

### 4.7.7 NOT Acute Stress Disorder

Window has long since closed. Mentioned only because his S1 post-liberation presentation, in real time, would have met ASD criteria; the diagnosis transitions to PTSD past the one-month mark.

### 4.7.8 NOT a Primary Psychotic Disorder

The auditory intrusions noted in 4.2.2 are trauma-typed intrusive recollections, not auditory hallucinations. They have first-person source attribution (he experiences them as *memories of Kilgrave's voice*, not as voices speaking now), they are content-specific to the trauma, they are mood-congruent, they have no associated formal thought disorder, no delusional elaboration, no negative symptoms. The distinction matters because misclassification would route him toward antipsychotic medication that would worsen the PTSD trajectory.

### 4.7.9 NOT a Bipolar Spectrum Disorder

No discrete elevated, expansive, or irritable mood episodes meeting duration criteria; no decreased need for sleep with preserved energy; no goal-directed activity beyond baseline (his S2-S3 productivity is steady, not episodic); no grandiosity; no pressured speech; no flight of ideas. His S3 hardening could be misread as hypomanic by an observer unfamiliar with moral-injury presentations. It is not.

### 4.7.10 NOT an Eating Disorder, Not OCD, Not GA


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS: MALCOLM DUCASSE

*An exhaustive catalog of observable behavior, micro-pattern, and decisional habit, derived from longitudinal canon (Jessica Jones S1-S3; The Defenders) and inferentially extended to the level of granularity a total-surveillance file would contain. Organized by state, with cross-references to etiology where relevant.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

The subject's calm baseline is not a "neutral" state but an *actively maintained* one - a curated equilibrium achieved through ritual, structure, and small acts of service. Pure idle calm is rare in the record and tends to migrate within minutes toward task, conversation, or caretaking.

**Postural baseline.** Upright but not stiff; shoulders held a touch forward of the spine - a habitual slight forward-lean that reads as attentive rather than slumped. When standing in a doorway or threshold (a recurrent micro-location for him - he is constantly being summoned into or out of rooms), he places one hand flat against the jamb at hip height, a stabilizing tic that predates the Kilgrave period and increases in frequency after it. When seated and listening, hands rest one-on-top-of-the-other on the thigh or steepled lightly at the sternum; when seated and thinking, he turns whatever object is nearest (pen, mug handle, phone) in a slow quarter-rotation.

**Vocal baseline.** Mid-register, slightly breath-light, with a counselor's cadence - sentences ending on a soft downturn that invites response rather than closes it. He does not interrupt. He uses the listener's name early in an exchange ("Jessica, listen-"; "Trish, hey-") more than peers do; this is a residue of clinical training and a comfort behavior. When relaxed, his diction becomes warmer and slightly more vernacular; when stressed, more careful, more clausal, more polysyllabic - he reaches for the educated register as armor.

**Verbal tics in calm.** "Hey." (greeting, soft, almost interrogative). "Okay, okay-" (twice, when accepting a task or absorbing news, a self-pacing device). "I'm just saying-" (when registering ethical concern he expects to be overridden). "Look-" (when about to take a stand he is not sure will hold). "Are you okay?" (the single most frequent question in his utterance set across the full record, asked of nearly every named figure he interacts with, often within ninety seconds of contact).

**Eye behavior.** Steady gaze during listening - the practiced gaze of someone trained to make people feel heard - with a characteristic small nod every three to five seconds at conversational pulse points. Breaks gaze upward and left when retrieving information; breaks gaze downward when retrieving feeling. With Jessica specifically, he holds eye contact a beat longer than colloquial norm, a pattern that reads as both attachment and supplication.

**Domestic / private rituals (inferred from canonically consistent pattern).** He keeps his space orderly to a degree his peers do not - dishes washed promptly, surfaces wiped, bed made on rising. This is post-Kilgrave overcorrection: during the captivity period his physical environment was filthy (canonically depicted on first discovery), and the order he now maintains is a daily small repudiation of that state. He showers long and twice-daily when his schedule permits; he keeps a clean rotation of dark, simple clothing (henleys, plain tees, dark jackets, dark jeans) that minimizes daily decision load and visually distances him from the ragged drug-period self.

**Reading and intake.** He still reads psychology - this is the surviving artifact of the abandoned vocation. He does not announce it. Books and articles accumulate on bedside and counter; he annotates margins lightly in pencil. He listens to news rather than music when alone, low volume, more for company than information.

**Eating.** Eats when offered; forgets when not. Drinks coffee black or with a single sugar; does not order elaborate food in public; pays for others' food more often than is reciprocated, a small chronic generosity that is also a small chronic ledger.

**Phone behavior in calm.** Picks up on the second ring (the first ring registers; the second confirms; he answers on the confirmation - a habit consistent with someone who once could not refuse a call). Texts in complete sentences with punctuation. Does not leave messages on read; replies within minutes when capable, with an apology when not.

---

## II. UNDER MILD STRESS (workload, deadline, mild interpersonal friction)

The first signs of stress arrive in his **hands** before his face. Pen-clicking, knuckle-press against the opposite palm, a brief two-finger rub at the bridge of the nose between brow and glasses-line (he does not wear glasses, but the gesture is anatomically located where they would sit - a vestigial movement, possibly from study-fatigue habits during undergraduate years).

**Verbal compression.** Sentences shorten. The counselor-cadence flattens. He still asks "are you okay?" but it becomes more functional, less inviting. The name-use drops; he addresses people by pronoun more.

**Increased helpfulness.** Counter-intuitively, mild stress *raises* his caretaking output. He will offer to get coffee, run an errand, "take that off your plate," reorganize a calendar - converting his own discomfort into others' relief. This is sublimation operating in real time and is the single most reliable predictor that he is, in fact, stressed: if Malcolm is suddenly extremely useful, something is wrong.

**Sleep degradation.** First behavioral casualty. He stays up later, ostensibly working; the laptop closes around 2-3 AM; he is up again by 7. Coffee intake increases by roughly one cup per stress-day. Visible signs lag by 48-72 hours: faint puffiness below the eyes, a slight grayness to the skin, a slowing of his usual quick smile.

**Withdrawal from frivolity.** Stops engaging with small-talk and humor; does not initiate, responds politely but briefly. His baseline warmth has a temperature drop of perhaps five degrees that intimates notice and acquaintances do not.

---

## III. UNDER MODERATE-TO-HIGH STRESS (active case pressure, moral ambiguity in current task, conflict with attachment figure)

This is the operational state he occupies most of S2 and S3 and where his behavioral signature is densest.

**The hardening sequence.** Observable in stages, reliably, in order:
1. *Quieting.* He talks less. The "are you okay?" disappears.
2. *Jaw set.* A small but persistent lateral tension at the masseter, sometimes accompanied by a slow exhale through the nose.
3. *Hand-stilling.* The fidgets stop. He becomes physically composed in a way that is *not* his baseline composed - it is held composure, a containment.
4. *Task narrowing.* He works in straight lines. Whatever is in front of him gets done in sequence with diminished commentary.
5. *Withdrawal from intimacy.* Calls and texts to non-task contacts (Trish, his parents in inferred off-screen pattern) drop or become curt.
6. *Acceptance of dirtier work.* Late in the sequence, he stops objecting to tasks he would have flagged a week earlier. This is the danger marker.

**The verbal tell of moral strain.** "I don't recognize myself" and its variants - "this isn't me," "I didn't used to-", "I never would have-". When this language appears, the moral injury is at threshold. He says it *aloud*, to others, which is itself the partial salvation: the words function as a flare. Operators who hear it and respond can recall him; operators who ignore it have a brief window before the next compromise locks in.

**Self-talk under pressure.** Audible muttering at low volume when alone or when he believes himself alone - usually a single word or short phrase repeated: "okay," "alright, alright," "come on, come on," "think." Pacing accompanies in confined spaces (apartment, office), three to five steps and turn.

**Decisional habits under moderate stress.**
- *He defaults to action over inaction.* Given a choice between waiting and moving, he moves. This is the counter-traumatic drive against helplessness and is one of the most exploitable patterns in his profile: an operator who needs him to act can usually engineer the conditions in which inaction *feels* like the Kilgrave state.
- *He accepts framing he should challenge.* When a request is presented as urgent and necessary by an attachment-relevant figure (Jessica, Trish, Hogarth), he tends to absorb the frame and work within it rather than question premises. He challenges premises in *retrospect*, often hours later, usually too late.
- *He segments.* He compartmentalizes tasks by client and by week, which lets him perform individually compromised acts without aggregating their moral weight. This is intellectualization in operational use.

---

## IV. UNDER THREAT (physical danger, ambush, confrontation with violent actor)

Malcolm is non-powered in a powered world; his threat behavior is calibrated to that reality.

**Initial response.** Brief freeze - perhaps half a second - followed by orientation: head turns toward sound or motion before body does. He looks for exits and for the location of any vulnerable third party (a witness, a victim, Jessica) before he assesses his own position. This is consistent with his caretaker orientation and persists even when self-preservation would dictate otherwise.

**Posture under threat.** Hands come up open-palmed and chest-height by default - a de-escalation default carried over from his clinical training - even when the threat is well past the point of verbal management. He has had to be physically pulled or shoved out of harm's way more than once.

**Verbal behavior in threat.** He talks. He talks fast. He uses the threatener's name if known, or asks for it. He narrates ("okay, okay, you don't have to do that, just-"). This is partly genuine de-escalation skill and partly an unconscious continuation of the helplessness defense: as long as he is *speaking*, he is not the silent compliant body Kilgrave made him.

**Willingness to take a hit.** He absorbs physical violence with notable composure - not bravery exactly, but a settled lack of surprise. The body has been instrumentalized once; pain has lost its novelty. He gets back up faster than is medically advisable. He does not, however, escalate to offensive violence easily; when he does strike, it is awkward, mechanically poor, and he stops short of follow-through.

**Tell: the after-tremor.** When the immediate threat passes, his hands shake. He hides them - pockets, behind back, gripping a hard surface. Breath catches once or twice. He will then ask the nearest person if *they* are okay, and only then sit down. This sequence is so consistent it can be treated as a signature.

---

## V. UNDER INTIMACY (sexual, emotional, disclosive)

**Sexual behavior.** Canonically established as comfortable with sex as instrument as well as as connection. With genuine partners he is attentive, generous, and verbally present (a relative rarity in his cohort); with instrumental partners (Trish in the period of mutual using) he performs competence without disclosure. The instrumental mode has a discernible somatic signature - slightly faster, less eye contact, a small post-coital withdrawal in which he is up and dressed inside ten minutes.

**Emotional intimacy.** He is *receptive* to others' disclosure to an extraordinary degree - he sits, he listens, he reflects, he does not flinch. His own disclosure is asymmetric: he will narrate facts of his history (the captivity, the addiction) with surprising matter-of-factness because the survivor-group context normalized the telling, but he will not narrate present-tense need. Ask him what *happened* and he answers; ask him what he *wants* and he deflects.

**The reciprocity asymmetry.** When someone attempts to care for him - to bring him food unprompted, to ask after his sleep, to express worry - he experiences a brief observable destabilization: an unsmoothed pause, a thank-you that lands slightly off, a redirect within a sentence or two back to the other person. He cannot be cared *for* without immediately reciprocating, and if reciprocation is refused (the other person insists on giving), he becomes briefly, mildly anxious. This is the most consistent intimacy tell in the record.

**Touch.** He touches others lightly and frequently in non-sexual contexts - a hand at the upper back guiding through a doorway, a brief squeeze of a shoulder when leaving a conversation, a knee-touch when sitting next to a distressed person. He receives touch from others well from women, more guardedly from men - the latter inflected by post-captivity wariness about bodily incursion.

**Sleep with another.** He sleeps poorly when sharing a bed for the first several nights with any partner. Wakes early. Leaves bed without waking partner. Makes coffee. This is not avoidance of the partner; it is a vigilance pattern, a small chronic check that the environment is what he left it as.

---

## VI. UNDER GRIEF (loss of person, loss of moral self-image, loss of attachment)

Malcolm grieves laterally rather than directly. He does not become inert; he becomes *busy on others' behalf.* In the immediate aftermath of loss he organizes - logistics of arrangements, calls to relevant parties, food brought to mourners, the practical scaffolding of grief in others.

**Personal grief signature.** Comes out at unexpected interstitial moments: alone in a kitchen at night, hand braced on the counter, breath held, then released slowly. A single exhalation that is the unit of his private mourning. He does not, on record, cry hard or for long; tears arrive briefly, are wiped quickly, and the face composes within seconds. This is not absence of feeling; it is the rapid containment of feeling so as to remain functional for whoever needs him next.

**Grief over the self.** The most pervasive grief in the record is the unspoken grief for the person he was before Kilgrave - the prospective clinical psychologist with intact faith and unfractured self-regard. He does not name this loss directly; it surfaces in the "I don't recognize myself" idiom and in occasional unguarded references to "what I was going to do" or "before I-" with the sentence trailing.

**Grief over Jessica's distance.** When pushed away by Jessica, his grief is anxious rather than depressive - increased reach-out behavior (texts, drop-bys), increased usefulness offered, a slight elevation in vocal pitch in her presence. He does not, in his canonical record, sulk or punish. He waits for the door to open and presents himself at it.

---

## VII. UNDER VICTORY (case closed, person saved, moral act completed cleanly)

Notably muted. He does not celebrate visibly. The face softens, the shoulders drop a quarter-inch, the smile - real, brief, slightly tired - appears and goes. He attributes credit outward: "you did it," "that was Jessica," "we got lucky." If pressed to accept credit, he accepts it with one syllable ("thanks") and changes subject.

**The post-victory ritual.** A long shower, often a walk, sometimes a call to his parents (inferred from established religious-family bond) in which the content of the case is not discussed but the contact itself reassures him that the version of himself who can call them still exists. He sleeps long the night after a clean victory - one of the few reliable indicators that he is at peace.

**Suspicion of victory.** Because his moral self-image is unstable, clean wins make him slightly uneasy. He looks for the catch, the cost, the part that will reveal itself later as compromise. He has a phrase he uses in these moments - some variant of "yeah, but-" - that signals he is not letting himself rest in the win.

---

## VIII. UNDER DEFEAT (case failed, person harmed on his watch, moral compromise visible to himself)

This is where his most concerning behavior lives.

**Immediate aftermath.** Silence first, then over-explanation. He will narrate the failure in detail to anyone who will listen - to Jessica, to Trish, to himself in the mirror in functional analog - parsing what went wrong, locating his own contribution, often *overstating* it. This is not self-pity; it is a forensic self-prosecution that he conducts in the absence of any external prosecutor.

**Behavioral drift after defeat.** He takes on more work, dirtier work, harder cases. This is the moral-injury recurrence cycle: the defeat confirms his diminished self-image, and from that diminished self he accepts tasks he would have refused from the intact self. The S3 arc is the longitudinal demonstration of this loop.

**Drinking.** Increases after defeat - moderately, never to the heroin-substitution level, but discernibly. Whiskey, neat, alone, slowly. Not enough to impair next-day function. Enough to register on a surveillance log.

**Withdrawal from his parents.** Calls home drop. He does not want to be the voice that arrives in their kitchen carrying what he carries. The drop in family contact correlates with moral-injury periods more reliably than almost any other metric.

**The sabotage move.** Under accumulated defeat he has been observed to sabotage relationships that are still functioning - small cruelties to people who do not deserve them, withdrawals from people who are still offering care. This is splitting against the self projected outward: if I am not who I was, then those who loved who I was should not love me, and I will help them stop.

---

## IX. WITH SPECIFIC FIGURES - INTERPERSONAL MICRO-PATTERNS

**With Jessica Jones.** Voice slightly softer. Stands closer than with others - within her arm's reach by default. Forgives faster than is healthy. Apologizes first in most disputes regardless of fault distribution. Watches her face for affect cues continuously - he reads her better than anyone else in the record and acts on those readings. Will lie to her selectively to spare her, then confess the lie later when the sparing is no longer necessary. Will not lie to her on matters of consequence even when self-protective. The asymmetry is total and known to both of them.

**With Trish Walker.** Warmer surface, less depth. He is one of the few people who treats her as a person rather than a celebrity or a project; she returns this with intermittent attention. Sexual chapter conducted with mutual instrumentality and mutual recognition of same; no observable lingering bitterness on his end. Subsequent interactions cordial, somewhat brotherly, with a residue of having known each other in a compromised state.

**With Jeri Hogarth.** Professional distance maintained verbally; physically he is uncharacteristically still in her presence - reduced fidget, reduced touch, a contained body. He reads her as dangerous (correctly) and performs reliability for her in a way that is half genuine and half costume. Disagrees with her in tactical detail, never in framework. When she pushes him toward a compromised act, his consent is delayed by perhaps two beats - the visible interval is the moral cost being calculated and absorbed.

**With Pryce Cheng.** Crisper, more transactional. He performs the harder version of himself with Cheng - speaks more briefly, smiles less, holds eye contact longer. This is partly mirroring (Cheng is a bare-knuckle operator), partly the experimental adoption of an instrumental self he is testing to see if it fits. It does not, quite.

**With his parents (inferred, from established family bond and from his own clinical-helper formation).** Reverts toward a younger register - vocabulary simpler, cadence softer, more "yes ma'am" / "yes sir" affect than peers would guess. Withholds catastrophically. They do not know about the heroin, the gun-adjacent work, the moral drift. He calls weekly when stable, monthly or less when not, and the call frequency is a leading indicator of his internal state.

**With the Kilgrave survivors group members.** Even, gentle, deliberately non-directive. He uses his clinical training overtly here and only here. Sits with hands open on knees. Mirrors body posture. Asks one question at a time and waits. This is the most undefended version of him in the canonical record - the closest to the person he was going to be before Kilgrave.

---

## X. DECISIONAL HABITS - GENERAL RULES OBSERVED ACROSS THE RECORD

- **He says yes faster than he should and revisits the yes later.** Initial compliance is high, secondary review is rigorous, and the gap between the two is where most of his trouble happens.
- **He accepts framing from attachment-relevant authority figures.** This is the most exploitable habit on his profile.
- **He resists *single* moral compromises poorly and *accumulated* compromises eventually but late.** The seventh ask is the one he refuses, after the first six have already cost him.
- **He privileges others' safety over his own without conscious weighing.** This is not heroism; it is the default state of the caretaker identity. He has to be reminded to consider himself.
- **He apologizes proactively.** When unsure of his standing in a relationship, he opens with an apology, often for things he has not actually done. The apology is a relational test - if accepted, he proceeds; if escalated, he reads the escalation as confirmation of his diminished worth and complies further.
- **He does not retaliate.** Across the entire record, with multiple objectively betrayal-meriting provocations, he does not retaliate against persons. He absorbs, withdraws, or redirects into work. The absence of retaliation is itself a signature.
- **He will not, under any condition observed in the record, take heroin again.** This is the one hard line. It is not a willpower question; it is an identity question. Returning to the drug would be conceding Kilgrave's continuing claim, and conceding that is something his entire post-S1 organization is structured to refuse.

---

## XI. SIGNATURE COMPOSITE

If a surveillance officer were given thirty seconds of footage and asked to identify Malcolm Ducasse with no audio, the cluster to look for is: a Black man in his late twenties to early thirties, dark plain clothing, standing in a doorway with one hand at the jamb, leaning forward slightly toward whoever is in the room, asking - we can lip-read it - *are you okay?* If the hand at the jamb is still and the jaw is set, he is in trouble. If the hand is moving and the face is open, he is, for the moment, himself.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

## SUBJECT: MALCOLM DUCASSE

---

## 1. THE GROUND TRUTH OF HIS DAYS

A week of continuous surveillance on Malcolm Ducasse would not produce the file of a chaotic man. It would produce, instead, the file of a man performing daily organization as therapy — a person who keeps the visible architecture of his life unusually tidy because the interior architecture is still load-bearing on damaged beams. His days are structured. They are also, on closer inspection, *over*-structured in the way that recovering people's days often are: routines do not merely organize his time; they *constitute* a portable scaffolding of self.

Two epochs must be tracked separately, because the daily shape changes substantially across the four-year canonical window:

- **Epoch A (post-withdrawal, S1 late through mid-S2):** convalescent rhythm, near-monastic, oriented around the survivor group and Alias Investigations.
- **Epoch B (mid-S2 through S3):** professional rhythm, oriented around Cheng's agency and then Hogarth's firm — more money, more clothes, more compromise, less sleep, less prayer.

The structural skeleton is constant. The flesh on it is what changes, and the changes are the surveillance product.

---

## 2. SLEEP, WAKING, AND THE FIRST HOUR

**Sleep onset.** Erratic. Records would show median bedtime drifting from approximately 23:30 in Epoch A to past 01:30 in Epoch B, with a long tail of nights ending closer to 03:00 during active investigative phases. He does not have a fixed pre-sleep ritual but has displaced rituals — reading on the couch, scrolling, sometimes a single beer (never two; the two-beer line is one he watches), occasionally a low-volume podcast. He almost never falls asleep in bed first; he falls asleep on the couch and migrates.

**Sleep architecture (inferred).** Light, easily interrupted, prone to one of two characteristic awakenings: (a) the 03:00-to-04:00 jolt — a brief, full-body wake with no apparent cause, after which he often gets up, drinks water, looks at his phone for 90 seconds, and lies back down for thin sleep until alarm; (b) the dream-into-bathroom transition — surveillance audio would capture him exhaling audibly on waking, sometimes a short low "hh-*hhh*" expulsion, the somatic register of a dream he will not narrate to anyone. He does not, on canon, talk in his sleep.

**Alarm and rise.** Alarm typically set 07:00–07:30; rises within five minutes of alarm in Epoch A, with a creeping snooze pattern in Epoch B (two or three taps, ten minutes apart, surrendering finally to the third). He sits on the edge of the bed for ~30–90 seconds before standing — a microbehavior that, on review, marks the daily transition from the unmonitored self to the public one. Lips often pressed; one hand on the back of the neck.

**First hour.** Bathroom, then a routine that in Epoch A includes a *brief moment of prayer or silence* — head bowed standing in the bathroom or sitting on the edge of the tub, eyes closed, between thirty seconds and two minutes, never longer. By late S3 this micro-ritual is intermittent and sometimes replaced by a longer, vacant look in the mirror that is no less ritualistic but no longer prayer. Brushes teeth thoroughly (~two minutes; he is the kind of person who watches the clock on his phone while brushing). Shaves every second day in Epoch A; in Epoch B, shaves daily, more carefully — a quiet upgrade in self-presentation that tracks the professional drift.

Hot water on the face. A particular small breath out as he leans on the sink. Then coffee.

---

## 3. INGESTION PATTERNS

**Coffee.** Heavy. Three cups by noon is the floor; five by end of day is the ceiling on hard days. Drip in Epoch A (Mr. Coffee on the counter, kept clean), pour-over equipment acquired in Epoch B. Black, occasionally with a splash of milk in winter. He associates coffee with competence and uses it as a self-administered nootropic; he does not associate it with pleasure, which is diagnostically interesting.
